However, in the time to come, the reasons for the Torah will also be revealed, as Rashi says on the verse, "Let Him kiss me with the kisses of His mouth"—"They are promised by Him to appear to them again to explain to them the secret of its reasons and its hidden mysteries"—in the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will teach Torah to all the people. Then, "Israel will be great sages and know the hidden things and will grasp the knowledge of their Creator according to the capacity of man, as it is said, 'For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea.'"

(From the Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Re'eh, 5747)


## ויקרא

## 183

### Vayikra

... And merit (purity and cleansing — and not only regarding oneself — [“You shall cleanse me”] —, but also — “and he shall cleanse the house.” Chullin 27a) is brought about on a meritorious day (and note what is written in many places at the end of section 11, that in our times there is no concern even to slaughter a goose in Teves) — the hillula of the Admur HaZaken, whose instruction, meaning the granting of strength — is that the shochet must be exceptionally G-d-fearing and trembles at the word of Hashem, complete in his knowledge, etc. (Hilchos Shechita 1:2. And see the discussion in Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, section 12).

[From a letter dated 24 Teves, 5725]

... Regarding your note on the words of our Sages, “If he had placed honey in it, etc., and why, etc., because, etc.” — for seemingly it should have said briefly: “One does not mix honey into it because, etc.” — it is resolved according to the Toras Kohanim on this verse, cited in Tosafos, s.v. “If he placed” (Kerisos 6a).

[From a letter dated 3 Menachem Av, 5720]

... Regarding what was written concerning the matter of “the verse repeated it to imply a requirement,” which could be explained as not being specific to kodshim — everything is by Divine Providence, and the letter was received when I learned that this sicha was being printed in HaMaor. And I requested to note the references to Tosafos Menachos 38a; Yad Malachi, Lekach Tov, rule 5. And see also Atvun D’Oraisa, rule 12.

And regarding the difficulty raised there (in Tosafos Pesachim 11a) — “such as kodshim” — and the Lekach Tov also addressed this — it is understood according to the aforementioned Tosafos in Menachos.

In Shitah Mekubetzes Zevachim (5a) — in the printing before me, it says “that they are merely a mitzvah regarding kashrus,” and this fits the continuation, “regarding acceptance,” meaning that the mitzvah is a category within the matter of kashrus or acceptance (and the category of requirement corresponds to it), and not a third matter added to the matters of kashrus and acceptance...

[From a letter during the days of Chanukah, 5720]


## ניסן

## 184

### Nissan

...May it be the will [of Hashem] that the command, "This month shall be for you," be fulfilled in each and every one of us, specifically as emphasized in Shemos Rabbah on this verse: "For *you* specifically," and in the manner explained in the maamar delivered at the farbrengen yesterday, based on the words of our Sages in the Yerushalmi: "A new wife—a new halacha," that they should innovate regarding the concept of creation, which is *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing), the opposite concept of *ayin miyesh* (nothing from something) (the explanation of the Tzemach Tzedek in the aforementioned).

And through this, the concept of "In Nissan they are destined to be redeemed" will also be fulfilled, as the Shemos Rabbah concludes on this matter, that [Rabbi Yehuda] follows his own reasoning: "Not with silver shall you be redeemed" (Sanhedrin 97b), as explained in the discourse *Hachodesh* of the summer of this year. And in this, too, there will be a miraculous occurrence: that although the male usually seeds first, representing *is'arusa d'le'eila* (see Likutei Torah from last week, *d.h. Shosh Asish*), nevertheless, she will bear a male [it is worth noting the Yerushalmi, Berachos, ch. 9, halacha 5, regarding one sitting on the birth stool, which differs from the Bavli there], for the future redemption is, in terminology, a "male" specifically (Pesachim 116b in Tosafos).
(From a letter of 28 Adar Sheni, 5717)

...Our Sages said (Rosh Hashanah 11a), "Rabbi Yehuda says: In Nissan they were redeemed, and in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed."

—And we hold according to Rabbi Yehuda that the redemption is in Nissan, based on the rule that between Rabbi Eliezer and Rabbi Yehuda, the halacha follows Rabbi Yehuda, as found in the sefer *Klalei HaShas*. See also Rashi and Tosafos in Rosh Hashanah (12a) regarding the Sages' statement "The flood was according to Rabbi Eliezer," where they write that since we count the *tekufos* according to Rabbi Yehuda, it follows that they hold like Rabbi Yehuda, etc. And in Tosafos, *d.h. Keman* (Rosh Hashanah 26a): "It is a difficulty, for this teaches us like Rabbi Yehuda," etc.

And even though we read the Haftorah on Shabbos Chol HaMoed Pesach regarding the day Gog comes (Megillah 31a), because the war of Gog will be in Tishrei (Tur Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, sec. 490), which seemingly implies that they hold that the redemption is in Tishrei, it can be said that this refers specifically to the war of Gog, which is the beginning of the days of Moshiach, as the verses prove and as is found in Rambam, *Hilchos Melachim* (ch. 12, sec. 2). But the redemption itself will be in Nissan. It is a matter requiring further study whether the redemption is before the war of Gog or after it. See Sanhedrin (97b): "The wars of Gog and Magog, and the rest are the days of Moshiach," and Rashi explains that the servitude ends and Moshiach comes. But in Avodah Zarah (3b) it seems the opposite, for it says there: "They do not accept converts in the days of Moshiach... but they become forced converts, because they see the war of Gog and Magog," etc. See also Vayikra Rabbah (ch. 30, sec. 5) that the days of Moshiach precede the war of Gog and Magog. Seemingly, it can be said that the redemption begins before

## 185

the war of Gog and Magog, but the redemption is not complete until after the downfall of Gog and Magog—and see Rashi *d.h. Atchalta* (Megillah 17b)—and what Rashi wrote (Sanhedrin, ibid.) "and Moshiach comes"—this refers to Moshiach ben Dovid, who comes after the beginning of the war of Gog and Magog, as is implied in Sukkah (52a). This is unlike Moshiach ben Yosef, who fights Gog and Magog; with him, the entirety of the days of Moshiach begins, and he precedes Gog and Magog. See also Yechezkel 38-39 and Zechariah 12-14. —It is a matter requiring study that in the Rambam, at the end of *Hilchos Melachim*, he omits the concept of Moshiach ben Yosef entirely, and it is implied from his language there that everything is accomplished by Moshiach ben Dovid.

And even according to Rabbi Eliezer, who holds that they are redeemed in Tishrei, Nissan is the month of redemption because the Exodus from Egypt occurred then, the first complete redemption...
(From a letter of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5704)

...And since we are moving (and in Chassidus, the precision of this language of our Sages is explained: that the Jewish person becomes a "walker," unlike before the descent of the soul below, when it is in a state of "standing") from the month of Adar, of which it is said, "The month which was turned for them" (and the precision of the language "the month" is that the *entire* month was turned) to joy, etc., to the month of Nissan, of which our Sages said (Shelah on the verse "This month") that every day of this month is in the category of Rosh Chodesh. And as the verse hints, "This month shall be for you the head of months," and Rosh Chodesh, even though work is permitted, is not included in the ordinary "days of action." As the verse (I Samuel 20) implies, the meaning is that the work done during these days is influenced by a more spiritual source, and consequently, the blessing is present in success to a greater degree (see *Or HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek 22a and onwards). Therefore, may it be the will [of Hashem] that from these months there be drawn down upon the entire year the concept mentioned: that in physical matters, the spirituality within them will be more highlighted, and consequently, the limitations and boundaries will diminish, until the prophecy is fulfilled: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders."
(From a letter of 9 Nissan, 5716)


## י"א ניסן

## 186

### 11 Nissan

**Blessing of the Rebbe to Anash who blessed him, 11 Nissan 5747, after Maariv**

1. May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the heartfelt requests for good of every single Jew, and especially those present here.
This is particularly relevant as we have a special power for this from the *zman shegrama* (the time-bound nature of this day):
We are in the month of Nissan, which has two *nun*s, signifying that "miracles of miracles were performed for him."
And within the month of Nissan itself—on the "eleventh day"—is the *Nasi* of the tribe of Asher. His matter is "he shall provide royal delicacies," the concept of *taanug*, and a level of *taanug* called "royal delicacies"—the *taanug* of a king. A king is generally accustomed to all good things. It is therefore understood that "royal delicacies" means a *taanug* that is (not merely more than the fulfillment of a lack, but) a *taanug* that is greater and in addition even to the expansion and perfection of the good to which a king is accustomed.

2. This (the matter of the month of Nissan in general, "miracles of miracles," and "on the eleventh day, the Nasi of the tribe of Asher") can be connected to *Chag HaPesach*—the general content and primary point of the entire month of Nissan:
The *Korban Pesach* (and in this time, the *Afikoman*, which is a remembrance of the *Pesach*) was eaten "at the end of the entire meal so that it would be eaten while satisfied, meaning that the *Pesach* should be the conclusion of the entire meal, so that they would enjoy its consumption... in a manner of importance and greatness... as kings and great people eat."
That is to say, that even before eating the *Korban Pesach* one has "satisfaction," and the *Pesach* adds to this even more pleasure and *taanug*—"royal delicacies," "as kings, etc., eat."

## 187

3. To this is added another point, and a novelty:
At the beginning of the *Seder* of *Pesach*, we proclaim: "Let all who are hungry come and eat, let all who are in need come and celebrate *Pesach*," and we conclude that all Jews become "free men."
And prior to this (beginning thirty days before the holiday) one gives to the poor of the city and in general "Maos Chittim."
This means that in addition to the fact that one must personally eat the *Pesach* "while satisfied" ("royal delicacies"), one must also give this to "all who are in need." One must give him not only "his needs" ("let all who are hungry come and eat"), but also "come and celebrate *Pesach*," the *Pesach* which is "eaten while satisfied," "as kings eat," "royal delicacies"—until one makes him a true "free man."
The reason for this is simple—because every Jew is a child of a king, and the only child of the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He.

4. Based on this, one can connect this to the chapter of *Tehillim* that many begin to recite on the eleventh day of the month of Nissan of this year:
The chapter begins with "I am poor and needy," and afterwards one continues "gladden the soul of Your servant."
It can be said that these are the two aforementioned extremes: one begins the *Seder* with "let all who are hungry, etc., let all who are in need, etc."—"poor and needy"; and one gives them the *Pesach* which is eaten while satisfied, "royal delicacies"—"gladden the soul of Your servant," the concept of *simcha* (joy) which is even greater than the fulfillment of a lack in general, and even greater than *taanug* in general, for *simcha* breaks through all boundaries.

## 188

5. And within this itself—there is an added emphasis when one stands immediately after *Maariv*, when the twenty-four-hour period of the "eleventh day" of the month of Nissan begins (according to *Torah* and *Shulchan Aruch*):
*Maariv* prayer is "optional." And it is explained in *Chassidus* that this is a higher *hemshech* (drawing down) than the *hemshech* that comes through "obligation." That is to say, in the *avodah* of man—not merely a *hemshech* of "his needs" (obligation), but a *hemshech* of "to enrich him" (optional).
It can be said that this is one of the reasons why Yaakov specifically instituted *Maariv*—because the "heritage of Yaakov" is a "heritage without boundaries."
To add, that in Yaakov there are also these two extremes: "Yaakov" is the letters *yud* and *akev* (heel). *Akev* (the lowest part of the body) refers to the level of "poor and needy." And into the level of *akev* ("poor and needy") is drawn the *yud*, from the highest heights (as the *Tzemach Tzedek* explains)—similar to "gladden the soul of Your servant," a breaking of boundaries (a heritage without boundaries), which is drawn down also to the "poor and needy."
Until the soul of Yaakov ("Yisrael Sava") is "included in all the souls in Israel from eternity to eternity," as explained in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe.

6. Therefore, it is appropriate—that standing now within the thirty days before *Chag HaPesach* (and in proximity to *Pesach*), when one has the obligation to give "Maos Chittim" to the poor,
And within the thirty days themselves—"on the eleventh day, the Nasi of the tribe of Asher," who "shall provide royal delicacies,"

## 189

And in a year when one begins to recite the chapter "I am poor and needy, etc., gladden the soul of Your servant,"
And on this day itself—immediately as one meets together at the beginning of the day, i.e., immediately after *Maariv* (optional), when "and there was evening" begins, which is the beginning (and hastens) to the "and there was morning," until it becomes "one day" (with all the interpretations thereof)—
One should give everyone a dollar, so that one should give it to a "poor and needy" person, so that for the "poor and needy" person there can be "eaten while satisfied" in all its details, and through this, there will also be *simcha* for him, "gladden the soul of Your servant."
And even if one has already provided for him—and certainly one has provided for him—that he should have "satisfaction" in all details, there is no limit to "satisfaction," it can always be more and more, especially when it concerns the nature of a Jew, a child of a king, and especially a child of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He.
And since all Jews are obligated in the *mitzvos* of *Pesach*, including the proclamation of "let all who are hungry come and eat, let all who are in need come and celebrate *Pesach*"—the matter (of giving a dollar so that it should be given to a "poor and needy" person) is relevant to all Jews, men, women, and even children.
On the contrary—children have a special connection with the "*Seder* of *Pesach*" and *Pesach* in general—as explained in many places that at the time of the Exodus from Egypt, Jews stood at the level of a "youth," like a minor, and because of this, the Exodus from Egypt occurred—due to the essential love of the Ribono shel Olam (the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He) for Jews as they are in the state of a "youth"—"When Israel was a youth (and therefore) I loved him,"
Similar to the great love and essential love that one has specifically for a "youth"

## 190

in the literal sense, children in years—as is known the *sicha* (*maamar*) on this from the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.* (which was said on *Simchas Torah*).

7. May it be His will that "as in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders" in this redemption (that is to come), and just as the Ribono shel Olam then took all Jews out of Egypt (due to His essential love for Jews), He will also take all Jews out of this *galus*, "and the children of Israel went out with a high hand,"
And in a manner of speed, haste—"He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye."
Especially as Jews are doing their *avodah* now (in the final days of *galus*) in a manner of speed and haste in all matters of holiness (which are all also matters of *simcha*), until in a manner of "He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye,"
Including in the aforementioned matter, that immediately at the beginning of "on the eleventh day" (immediately after *Maariv*, which Yaakov instituted) in a manner of "He did not delay them"—one gives every Jew, man, woman, and child, a dollar to bring "satisfaction" and *simcha* to a "poor and needy" person (as mentioned above).
This will further hasten the speed and haste of the future redemption, and in a manner of breaking the boundaries of time (since this comes through the *avodah* of "gladden"), and "a heritage without boundaries," the heritage of Yaakov (who instituted *Maariv* as optional),
Together with the building of the Third *Beis HaMikdash*, which is called a "house" (because it will be an eternal house), corresponding to Yaakov (the "chosen of the Patriarchs"), as the Sages say, "Not like Avraham, of whom it is written 'mountain,' nor like Yitzchak, of whom it is written 'field,' but like Yaakov, whom they called 'house'."

## 191

And similar to this—Jews have even in the final moments of *galus*, "as in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt" when "all the children of Israel had light in their dwellings" while still in *galus*,
And in a manner of *simcha* and goodness of heart, together with children, life, and abundant sustenance—abundant, which also includes the matter of *taanug*,
And *taanug* and all these matters—simply and plainly below ten *tefachim*, as souls in bodies during the time of *galus*.
And afterwards, immediately go dancing to the preparations for *Chag HaPesach*, kosher and happy,
And to the "time of our freedom"—the true and complete redemption—which comes even before *Pesach*, and consequently, freedom is added in a manner of "going and increasing and light," until the freedom of *Chag HaPesach*,
And through *simcha* and goodness of heart, and in this too—going and increasing and light.
[The Rebbe gave everyone—men, women, and children—a dollar bill to give to *tzedakah* (or its equivalent).]

## 192

**Blessing of the Rebbe to Anash who blessed him, eve of Tuesday, Parshas Shemini, 11 Nissan 5748, before Maariv**

May the promise of the Holy One, Blessed be He, be fulfilled in everyone, within all of Israel, that "whoever blesses is blessed" with the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, whose "addition is greater than the essence," and—"from His full, open, holy, and wide hand," to each and every one, within all of Israel, in everything they need,
Until the main matter (as mentioned)—the true and complete redemption through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*.
Especially as this (the redemption) is a matter that is time-bound,
Both from the perspective of the month, the month of Nissan—as the promise of the *Torah* of truth and *Torah* of life, that "in Nissan they were redeemed and in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed";
Both from the perspective of the week—Tuesday, on which "it was good" was doubled, as the redemption is the perfection of good, until doubled good, good for Heaven and good for creatures, as they stand unified in one reality (at every moment of Tuesday);
And both from the perspective of the year—the year 5748 (Tashmach), and also a year of *Hakhel*, "Assemble the people, the men, the women, and the children," for the perfection of *simcha* and the perfection of *Hakhel* will be in the future redemption—"everlasting joy upon their heads," and "a great congregation shall return here."
The timing makes the time even more prepared for the true and complete redemption, and all Jews go, "a great congregation shall return here," to our holy land, and one goes with speed—"He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye," "with the clouds of heaven."

## 193

And one has the perfection of the land, together with "Hashem your G-d will expand your border"—all ten lands and nations (in addition to the seven, also the three lands of the Keini, Kenizi, and Kadmoni),
Together with the perfection of the people of Israel, a "great congregation" of "the men, the women, and the children" (as above), and in each type separately—the perfection of every detail and detail within the detail, in the minutiae, and on the other hand: everyone as a detail (remaining a separate reality) becomes a part of the "great congregation," until even more—as the Baal Shem Tov says that the essence, when you grasp a part of it, you grasp the whole of it.
And the perfection (of the people of Israel) also acts upon the entire world, which also consists of division, "How manifold are Your works," "How great are Your works," until a division without end—it becomes together with this revealed to all eyes that the world (and all its details) is a private domain for the One of the world, and in a manner of "And your Teacher shall no longer be hidden, and your eyes shall see your Teacher," as explained in the holy *Tanya*.
And furthermore, and this is the main thing—and He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye, immediately and instantly, truly.
[One of the *rabbonim* of Anash blessed the Rebbe with *Birchas Kohanim*, and the Rebbe said:]
And after the resurrection of the dead, when "Moshe and Aharon will be with them," every Jew and all Jews—as part of the essence of a great congregation—will hear all these matters and blessings—a great blessing—from Aharon the High Priest, in the Third *Beis HaMikdash*—a great house.

## 194

**Blessing of the Rebbe to Anash who blessed him, Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, eve of 11 Nissan 5749, after Maariv and Havdalah**

First of all—"whoever blesses is blessed" with the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, whose "addition is greater than the essence," and below ten *tefachim*, and immediately and instantly—from His full, open, holy, and wide hand.
And may it be fulfilled in every Jew and in all Jews, within all of Israel, the "song, a psalm of the sons of Korach, for the Conductor" (the chapter of *Tehillim* 88 appropriate for this year)—as discussed at length earlier: in every Jew and in all his matters, physical and spiritual—there should be a "song, a psalm," a song with the mouth—which includes all matters of the soul (and through the soul), and a psalm with an instrument—which includes all matters of the body (and through the body), until also his portion in the world—all the possessions of a person (which are like an instrument that a Jew uses for the sake of the Ribono shel Olam),
And both modes of *avodah* ("song, a psalm") are "of the sons of Korach"—in them is accomplished the elevation of *teshuvah*, until *teshuvah ila'ah* (higher repentance), which is with great *simcha*,
Until accomplishing the matter of "for the Conductor"—that there should be a complete victory of every Jew, and of all Jews, and of all Jews together—the victory of carrying out what the Ribono shel Olam wants, and what every Jew wants, and what all Jews want,
Until the most essential matter—that immediately and instantly, and He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye, the true and complete redemption should come through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, David the King, *Mashiach*.


## חג הפסח. עניני פסח

## 196

### Pesach. Matters of Pesach

...Regarding the note on what was written in the Kehot Haggadah, 2nd edition, that generally the three matzos are *keilim* (vessels) and the six items [on the seder plate] are *oros* (lights): this can be explained based on what is written in many places, that Ze'er Anpin and Malchus are analogous to *ohr makif* (surrounding light) and *keilim*, and in *keilim* there are inner, intermediate, and outer [vessels].
(From a letter dated 7 Adar, 5720)

"Fifteen" *Dayeinu* and "goodness" (*Dayeinu*): the fifteen is "and build for us the Beis HaBechirah," and on the contrary, it is the main point, "to atone for all our sins."
The version I mentioned is for the sake of sharp analysis, as is simple.
(From a letter, Tammuz 5750)

...Regarding what was discussed, that there is a debate concerning one who eats chametz on Pesach: even though he has transgressed a Torah prohibition, he nevertheless fulfills the positive commandment of "you shall remove" (*tashbitu*) and eliminates the prohibition of "it shall not be seen" (*bal yeira'eh*)—I found a note in my records that this is stated in *Sefer Teshuvah Me'ahavah*, section 182, and not like the *Ta'am HaMelech* on Rambam, *Hilchos Chametz U'Matzah*, Chapter 1, Halacha 3. I do not have the book before me now.
—And the *Hasagos* of the Ra'avad and the Ramban on the *Baal HaMaor* (to the Rif, first chapter of *Pesachim*)—one can interpret their opinion as being that it is forbidden to eat, but if one transgressed and ate, he has fulfilled the positive commandment, etc.
(From a letter, 12 Shevat 5765)

## 197

...There is no answer to your question regarding wine for the Arba Kosos. When you speak with your doctor, he will permit you to make juice from cooked grapes. Ask him whether it is better with sugar (naturally, Pesach-dik sugar) or entirely without sugar. Orange juice is not to be considered at all for use for the Arba Kosos...
(From a letter, 10 Adar, 5720)


## אחרי

## 244

### Acharei

... Regarding the general matter of adoption, it is surprising that I have not yet found anyone who has paid attention to the following point. Although several responsa have already been published detailing various laws that arise from the matter of adoption, no one has raised an issue with the fundamental concept itself, etc.

The concerns that have arisen for me are that adoption in our current times is not like it was in previous generations, where one fulfilled the mitzvah of raising an orphan in one’s home, etc., where the entire environment—including the child being raised—knew that these were not his biological parents. Now, it is the opposite: they do everything possible to conceal this detail. Furthermore, due to pressure from doctors—who claim to be experts in matters of the psyche—they decide that it is forbidden to reveal this to the child (because it might damage his peace of mind, etc.). The result of this is that their conduct with the adopted child is as if he were their own biological child, which inevitably leads to all the issues of *yichud*, hugging, kissing, etc., every single day. And it is certainly impossible to be careful about this, even if the adoptive parents are truly *yirei shamayim*.

Even if they do reveal to the adopted child when he grows up that these are not his parents, it is highly questionable whether it is possible to change a pattern of behavior that has existed for many years prior. Based on what has been said, there is certainly a *d'rabbanan* prohibition, and according to the Rambam, there is also a *d'oraysa* prohibition. And even regarding a *d'rabbanan* prohibition, it is different when it is a matter that is repeated and tripled, etc. (in addition to what is brought and explained in the books of *nigleh* regarding this—see also *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our *Alter Rebbe*, Chapter 7). Seemingly, based on the above, the entire matter of adoption is highly questionable. The reason for leniency in such cases—that it is better that they be *shogegin* (unintentional sinners), etc.—is seemingly clear, as many would refrain from adoption if they knew the above. See also *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, siman 608, and the *Shulchan Aruch* of our *Alter Rebbe* there, regarding the various parameters of "better that they be," etc.—based on which the leniency of "better that they be," etc., is not clear in the case at hand. And certainly, for someone of your stature, further elaboration is unnecessary.

(From a letter dated 21 Shevat, 5724)

... The *psak din* from the *Tzemach Tzedek* is found in *Sefer Shaarei Deah*, siman 61. The *Tzemach Tzedek* is also mentioned there in siman 62 (in *Choshen Mishpat*), 91.

To say that the source for the Rambam’s statement (*Hilchos Issurei Biah*, 15:15) that the son of a *niddah* is blemished is from *Maseches Kallah*, and similarly in the *Biur HaGra* to *Shulchan Aruch Even HaEzer*, 4:13—this is highly questionable to me, as, on the contrary, that source is proof

## 245

to the contrary, since it was established specifically according to the words of Rabbi Akiva that he is a *mamzer* and the son of a *niddah*, and they said that Rabbi Akiva was great because he refuted the words of those who disagreed with this...

(From a letter dated 29 Adar, 5721)

... I acknowledge receipt of your letter (in addition to the list of *Chiddushei Torah* from your honor—which arrived earlier). It is well known that I do not involve myself in *psak din*, etc., especially in a matter that many have already debated. I ask for your forgiveness.

P.S.
According to our Sages in *Pirkav d'Oraisa*: Like the opinion of the Rambam (*Sefer HaMitzvos*, negative commandment 346) that "You shall not lie with your neighbor's wife," etc., is a warning to the man only, so too in the *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol* (negative commandment 97) (and apparently in *Sefer Yereim*, siman 214, it should also read: "Our Creator warned us regarding the adulterer"—not "adultery"—as it appears in the printed editions). And in the *Chinuch*, mitzvah 35, it says "and this negative commandment is doubled," and in the *Minchas Chinuch* there, it says "they warn him with this negative commandment here or with the negative commandment of 'you shall not lie'." Based on this, the explanation that this applies specifically to the man is missing.

Regarding the words of the Ramban (*Acharei* 18:20): "And it is possible that he said," etc., the reason for the prohibition is highly questionable as to whether one can learn from this regarding *halacha*, because: 1) He concludes that this reason does not apply to *halacha* (for punishment). 2) He retracts and writes: "And the correct view in my eyes is that it is because," etc. (and he does not write: "and one could also say" or something similar). 3) He concludes there: "And our Sages expounded"—meaning our Sages of the *halacha* in the Torah.

(From a letter written in the year 5725)


## קדושים

## 245

### Kedoshim

...Regarding your note about the special importance of the *middah* of *ahavas Yisrael*—for even among the nations of the world, an Englishman loves the English, etc., and one must distinguish between Yisrael and the nations—the fundamental difference is understood from the language of the verse, "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself." Just as a person’s love for himself is not dependent on his seeing his own virtues—whether in intellect, *middos* of the heart, or in thought, speech, and action; on the contrary, "love covers all transgressions"—so too is the command regarding the love of one’s neighbor: it must also be a self-love that is not dependent on any thing or any virtue, etc.

Based on this, the wonder is understood: how can the level of love for another be "as yourself"? Regarding this, our *Rabbeinu HaZaken* provides an explanation in *Tanya*, Chapter 32. He begins his explanation with the level of love for another that is easier to attain, "for who knows their greatness and virtue," etc. Yet, ultimately, this is still a love dependent on virtue. Therefore, he adds the explanation, "that they are all equal, and one Father for them all," etc., "truly brothers." See there.

## 246

A special emphasis on all the aforementioned, according to the teachings of *Chassidus*, is explained in *Sefer HaMitzvos* by the *Admur HaTzemach Tzedek*, *Mitzvas Ahavas Yisrael*, Chapter 2. See there.

We connect matters to appropriate times, for we are currently in the *Bein HaMetzarim* of the destruction of the Second *Beis Hamikdash*, which occurred because of *sinas chinam* (baseless hatred). It is simple that we were commanded to make a remembrance for the destruction, especially in these days, with the intention of *tikkun* (rectification). For the destruction is, as the text of the *tefillah* states, "And because of our sins we were exiled from our land," etc., and it is impossible to nullify the effect except by nullifying the cause. Any deficiency or weakness in the cause brings about a deficiency and weakness in the effect, even if it is—as explained in the teachings of *Chassidus*—for the time being only in the upper worlds. And since the primary sin, as our Sages of blessed memory have informed us, was *sinas chinam*, its *tikkun* is *ahavas chinam*—that is, a love that is not dependent on anything. May it be the will that we merit very soon the end of our exile and the true and complete *Geulah* through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, and may these days be transformed into joy and gladness.
(From a letter of 5 Menachem Av, 5724)

...Regarding what you wrote about the third birthday of your son, *shlita*, which falls on Rosh Chodesh Shevat, and your initial thought to perform the haircut on Lag B'Omer: I have already written my opinion to several of *Anash* that if there is no strong reason—such as a fixed and well-established custom—it seems to me that one should not delay the haircut, especially for several months or even several weeks. My reasoning is that since it is apparent from the language of *Kvod Kedushas Moreinu V'Rabbeinu HaAdmur* regarding the "holiday of the haircut" that this is a matter of *chinuch* in *yiras Shamayim*—that is, the drawing down of *kedushah* upon the soul of the child [it is possible that the aforementioned is based on the well-known statement of our Sages (Tanchuma, Parshas Kedoshim), and see also *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by *Rabbeinu HaZaken* at the beginning, that this is hinted at in the Written Torah, "And in the fourth year all its fruit shall be holy," etc.], and when one performs an action in this, the matter is strengthened and drawn down into the world of action, as explained in many places—why should one delay this drawing down of *kedushah* for several months or weeks? For every addition of *kedushah* in *chinuch* adds to all matters of the child, and even the physical.
(From a letter of 26 Kislev, 5717)

...Regarding your question as to when to perform the haircut of your son, *shlita*: although it is clear in my opinion that one should not do it before he reaches the age of three, regarding doing it three days later, as in your case where the birthday is 13 Nissan—if they extend it by three days, it will naturally be delayed and performed at the *tziyun* of *Rashbi*—you should consult with the *rabbanim* of *Anash* in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.
(From a letter of 2 Teves, 5721)

...Regarding your question about the haircut of your son, *shlita*: since it falls in the winter days, there is a concern that the sudden change from a large amount of hair to a precise haircut might cause a cold, *chas v'shalom*, etc., and therefore your initial thought was to delay it for some time.

In my opinion, this is not correct, because from the well-known language of *Kvod Kedushas Moreinu V'Rabbeinu HaAdmur* regarding the haircut of three years, it is implied that there is in this a drawing down of *kedushah*, an addition of *kedushah* to the soul of the child through the leaving of the *peios*, etc. Why should one delay this drawing down? On the other hand, there is no necessity for a precise haircut; one can leave longer hair for the time being, provided that the matter of leaving the *peios* is recognizable. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant success to you and your wife, *shichyu*, to raise him to Torah, *chuppah*, and good deeds, with proper health and *harchavas hada'as*.
(From a letter of 27 Teves, 5717)

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Bereishis, and by way of introduction, it is understood and simple that there is no place here for a request for forgiveness or the like, for the letter speaks of words of Torah, and especially of matters that relate to practice. You are also correct in the conclusion of your letter, that this is a matter that concerns many, since it is seen by many.

Regarding the content of the question or the note: the conduct you write of—that is, not to touch the *peios* of the head at all—I have not seen within *Chabad*, and on the contrary.

It is possible to suggest several reasons for this, and perhaps also the reason hinted at in your letter, not to mix the *oros* of two *tikkunim* from the thirteen *tikkunim* of the *Dikna Kadisha*. In any event, it is explicit that the *Arizal* would cut and shorten them with scissors (*Shaar HaMitzvos* and *Taamei HaMitzvos*, Parshas Kedoshim).

According to the above, the instruction of our Sages applies to this, a clear instruction, in *Maseches*... as we follow (*Sukkah* 32b): "Rav Acha bar Rava would turn... and one, since it went out from the mouth of Rav Kahana." See there in Rashi. And if you say so, it is *kal v'chomer* in our case, where it is not only the word of the *Rav* but *maaseh rav* (the action of the *Rav*).
With respect and blessing.
According to the above, it is explained that the question and wonder is, on the contrary, regarding those who do not touch them at all—

## 248

the opposite of the *maaseh rav* of the living *Arizal*. See also *Darchei Teshuvah* to *Yoreh Deah*, section 81, that these are laws, etc. And in *Darchei Chaim V'Shalom*, 546, that one should not tuck the *peios* behind his ear (indeed, what the compiler points out there to *Zohar Chadash*, etc.—it requires study, for as it is understood simply—in *Zohar Chadash*, etc., it is speaking of hair that grows behind the ear).
(From a letter of 26 Tishrei, 5721)

In response to your letter from Tuesday, in which you write about the matter of clothing.

It is strange that you have doubt about this, at the same time that you bring in your letter both the sayings of our Sages and the legal rulings that obligate the matter. See also *Shu"t Admur HaTzemach Tzedek*, *Yoreh Deah*, section 91 (and the omission to the aforementioned at the end of *Shaar HaMiluim* there), based on the verse (Zephaniah 1:8).

As for your note regarding what is written in *Likutei Dibburim* in the explanation of the saying of our Sages that they did not change their clothing, that this relates to the beard and *peios*—it is simple that the aforementioned is in addition to what was said, for this saying does not depart from its simple meaning: clothing literally, external clothing.
(From a letter of 21 Menachem Av, 5721)

...Regarding what you wrote about the reason for growing a beard, it is explained at length according to the *nigleh* in *Shu"t HaTzemach Tzedek*, *Yoreh Deah*, section 93, and according to the *pnimiyus haTorah* in *Peirush HaMilos* by the *Tzemach Tzedek* on the verse "And He, being merciful, forgives iniquity," printed in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Part Two, and in the *Miluim* to *Tehillim* with the commentary of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, page 626. See his words there, for they are pleasant, and how much this matter relates especially to *bochurim*.
(From a letter of 25 Teves, 5716)

After your long silence, your letter from Sunday was received. Regarding what you write about the beard, it is understood that your words are refuted, for our *Nasi* says that the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* are a channel for *hashpaah* (influence) to a person and his household, and *hashpaah* with mercy and great mercy (see on this in *Peirush HaMilos* by *Kvod Kedushas Admur HaTzemach Tzedek* on the verse "And He, being merciful," also printed in the *Miluim* to *Tehillim*, *Yahel Ohr*).

## 249

With a blessing for the recognition of your true situation—that is, that He who feeds and sustains all will provide enough for your livelihood and the livelihood of all your household, *shichyu*, in a kosher manner and in a *chassidishe* manner, and especially through the aforementioned thirteen *tikkunei dikna*. Consequently, you yourself will be amazed and also distressed by this: "Why does one waste nerves and health on baseless worries?" It is understood that this is not a contradiction at all to what is written, "in all your ways," but it must be according to the precise language of our Sages: "When you eat the labor of your hands"—that is, only the labor of the hands, also in the spiritual sense, meaning the power of action and *hishtadlus* (effort), but not the labor of your head—that is, worries and troubles of the head regarding this. There is no need to elaborate on a matter that is simple and explained in many places.
(From a letter of Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5716)

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, in which you write in connection with a wedding in the family, and the bride requests that at least until the wedding the father should remove his beard, and if not, etc.

Although in general this is not the way to answer one person regarding matters that concern another, and especially since in most cases it is impossible for another to know the situation in all its details, and certainly not to know what is in the heart of the other—nevertheless, due to the great wonder, I have come to respond. The wonder is twofold:

1) That an adult person—for she is already a bride—would base her relationship with her father, and publicly, on the fulfillment of a demand such as this. I will emphasize how far things have reached, that she is publicizing the demand, etc.

2) That the matter concerns a *Chabad* family, who certainly know (or at least should know) that according to the *Nesi'im* of *Chabad*, the matter of growing a beard is a matter of *halacha*. Furthermore—and this is also important—there is a special *segulah* in this for the drawing down of the blessing of *Hashem* in abundance, as explained at length in the writings of *Admur HaTzemach Tzedek*. Every day and in every case, a person is in need of the blessing of the Creator of man, the Creator of the world and its Guide. Certainly, in a fundamental way, one is in need of blessing at the time of laying the foundation for an eternal edifice, such as a wedding and marriage. And precisely in connection with the *chuppah* and marriage, they come with a demand and a claim, and in an ultimatum, that he should do the opposite of what is stated, *chas v'shalom*!

I must add another point regarding the matter itself, even if it were a matter of non-Jews—to distinguish—for the fashion has spread in recent years to grow a beard, and from period to period those who do so increase, and (in the style of your letter) they are viewed as respectable people.

I do not know the extent of your influence on the aforementioned, but our Sages of blessed memory said, "Accept the truth from whoever says it." May it be the will that you succeed in explaining to the aforementioned the strangeness of the whole matter and its lack of logic, in addition to the point from the *halachic* side here, and especially since her father has been accustomed to growing a beard for a long time.

It is understood that the above does not relate to combing the beard with a suitable comb, as the *Rav* in their neighborhood will explain.

## 250

According to your letter about your family and origin, my hope is that in the spirit of *Chabad* families, you are active in spreading traditional Judaism in your surroundings and wherever your hand reaches. We have been promised that words that come from the heart enter the heart of the listener and perform their action.

With a blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.
(From a letter of 2 Tammuz, 5725)

...And regarding your question about the haircut, etc.—since I have not heard an explicit instruction on this, there are sides to both directions. Therefore, clarify the custom of *Anash* in this with the *rabbanim* of *Anash* who know the conduct in practice from the elder *Chassidim*, and *maaseh rav* (the action of the *Rav*).
(From a letter of 5 Elul, 5720)


## אמור

## 250

### Emor

... Regarding what you noted in Bechoros 41a — based on what Rabbeinu Gershom writes there, the proof is from the fact that *cheres* (earthenware) implies *charutz* (a groove/incision), as the letters *samech* and *tzadi* are interchangeable.

Based on this: 1) We can understand the statement in the Gemara: "Since the Master said, 'A *gerev* is a *cheres*'" (for on the face of it, what is the superiority of *cheres* over *gerev*?). 2) It must be that *nega* (a plague/spot) is [defined by depth], etc. — this comes to prove that there is room here for an interchange, since in all *nega'im* it must be "deeper than the skin" (even though for the sign of *tumah*, it is sufficient if its appearance is deep, rather than its physical substance). See further on this in *Torah Temimah* to *Tazria* 13:3.

[quotation](From a letter from the days of Selichos, 5719)[/quotation]


## ל"ג בעומר

## 251

### Lag B’Omer

B’H, Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5747.
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To all the children of Yisrael,
May Hashem grant that they live,
Peace and blessing!

It is surely known to you that every important task that must be done requires preparation well in advance, so that the matter is carried out properly.

We stand on the eve of the month of Iyar, the month in which there is a most important day, Lag B’Omer, the eighteenth (Chai) of Iyar, a day for which special customs have been established for children,

## 252

and also to influence others to do the same, in accordance with the command of the Ribono shel Olam, "Love your fellow as yourself."

Therefore, it is appropriate that each and every one of you prepare for this by beginning to study the aforementioned instructions and good deeds. On the day of Lag B’Omer, the day of his "simcha"—as Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai referred to this day—you should hold a gathering in his honor and perform all that has been mentioned, all of you together. Furthermore, you should organize a parade in your place of residence to publicize even more your connection with the Torah through Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, for whom "his Torah was his craft" (Torah was his primary occupation).

You should ask your parents and educators, may they live, to assist you in all of this, in accordance with the command of the Torah that is about to be read on Erev Lag B’Omer in all synagogues everywhere: "Speak... and you shall say," as our Sages of blessed memory interpret: "to warn the adults regarding the children."

Great is the merit of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai—to bring success to each of you in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, and all of this with simcha, including everything mentioned above, and to merit very soon to see, "You are the G-d who performs wonders"—"I will show him wonders"

## 253

in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.
With the blessing of Rosh Chodesh and for great success,
[Signature]

B’H, Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled,
Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5747.
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To all Jewish parents and to all Jewish educators,
May Hashem grant that they live,
Peace and blessing!

Based on the Torah’s command, "One only encourages the encouraged," and as the virtue of *zerizus* (zeal) and its necessity are known in all matters of Yiddishkeit, and especially in carrying out the Torah’s threefold command "to warn the adults regarding the children"—the foundation of true chinuch—including also the content of the attached letter "To all the children of Yisrael," shlita.

The letter is accompanied by a heartfelt request to assist, encourage, and expedite all matters in the letter, especially the holding of the gathering and the organizing of the parade. This will surely add even more to the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam—to derive true *nachas* from each of the children, a *nachas* permeated with the inwardness of Torah as explained in the Zohar, the "chibura dilach" (your composition) of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, the master of the simcha of Lag B’Omer.

May it be the will that all this will further hasten the promise in the Zohar: "Through this composition of yours, which is the Sefer HaZohar... they will emerge from galus with mercy," speedily in our days, truly.

With respect and the blessing of great success in all this, and with the blessing of a good month,
[Signature]

## 254

B’H, Sunday, Parshas Bechukosai,
Tiferes sheb'Hod,
5749. Brooklyn, N.Y.
To all the sons and daughters of Yisrael,
Wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant that they live,
Peace and blessing!

As we stand in the period of the "seven complete weeks," and within it, the Shabbos of Lag B’Omer, and within the beginning of the "three days" of this auspicious day, in which surely each and every one is awakened to an increase in Torah and mitzvos, especially in connection with this day—and particularly since this year it falls on a Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, "good for Heaven and good for the creations"—I am here to awaken [you] regarding the suggestion of many and their decision to act upon it in actual deed, for the deed is the essential thing:

To increase in Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim—upon which the world stands. And regarding Rashbi, it is said, "And a Tzaddik is the foundation of the world."

## 255

Giving to tzedakah in the amount of "Chai"—for Lag B’Omer is the 18th (Chai) of Iyar (the initials of Avraham, Yitzchak, Yaakov, Rachel—which includes all four Matriarchs).

In avodah—Psalm 33 in Tehillim, the book of prayers of Dovid ben Yishai, the "pleasant singer of the songs of all the children of Yisrael."

In Torah—in the weekly parsha, and especially in the part specific to this day, the third day: "And you shall eat... and I will place My Sanctuary among you (within each and every one)... and I will lead you upright."

May the aspiration be fulfilled: "May my prayer come before You, incline Your ear to my cry," for Hashem—as Rashbi states—is always with each one wherever they may be. He will immediately fulfill the promises: "I have found Dovid My servant," and "I will place My Sanctuary among you"—this is the Third Beis Hamikdash, "the Sanctuary, O Hashem, that Your hands have established."

And our Torah, the Torah of life, has taught a lesson for the life of every single day: "Rashbi is worthy to be relied upon in times of distress"—the galus—"and they are immediately redeemed."

## 256

With respect and blessing, and as Rashbi requires—to participate in his great simcha of Lag B’Omer—"in one bond I am bound to Him, to the Ribono shel Olam; in Him I am attached, to Him I am joined, to Him I am cleaved"—and in a manner of "a candle to illuminate"—an influence in this upon one's entire surroundings, men, women, and children.
[Signature]

P.S. It is understood and simple that even after Lag B’Omer, one must continue to do and complete all of the above, as we learn from Pesach Sheni, from which we derive: "Nothing is lost," and with double the strength.


## בהר

## 257

### Behar

I received your letter of 21 Sivan with thanks, and subsequently, your two books, *Hilchos Shemitas Karka’os* and *Sefer Karvah Shenas Hasheva*, were also received.

Many thanks for your detailed letter and for your thoughtfulness in sending me the aforementioned works.

Although time does not permit me to examine the matters you write about in the necessary detail—especially to reconcile them with what is written in *Sefer La’or Hahalacha* and elsewhere—seemingly, it is difficult to understand why, regarding trees, the matter of selling the land for a limited time is not also mentioned. Since the labors performed in the manner you describe require a basis for leniency, and many great authorities hold that a sale for a limited time is effective in this regard, by doing so, one would also save those who, despite the instructions, will perform labors that were not permitted—and who, unfortunately, are found everywhere, for one labor leads to another...

(From a letter dated 25 Tammuz, 5717)

With great astonishment and even greater sorrow, I read your letter, which you begin with praise to the Almighty, as you count (Heaven forbid) on traveling to Eretz Yisrael on a ship whose owners are Jews, and the captain, the sailors, the entire crew, and the service staff are all Jewish, or 99 percent of them are Jewish; and you continue your writing by saying that the merit of our holy forefathers should bring success to the journey!

I would have thought it unnecessary to explain the reason for my great sorrow, but the content of your letter compels me to write at least a few lines about it, although no matter how much one were to write about this, it would be little in comparison to the gravity of the matter. In short:

A journey on such a ship—for every passenger, not to mention the crew employed on the ship—is: a) a desecration of Shabbos, b) in public (*b'farhesia*), c) participating in a *chillul Hashem* in public (also before all the non-Jews) who know of the aforementioned, d) this is done in the name of the entire Jewish people,

## 258

whose contributions on various occasions have helped the operation and functioning of the ship on Shabbos.

It should also be added that it is a rare opportunity to desecrate Shabbos in public every moment of the twenty-four hours of Shabbos Kodesh, even when one is sleeping! For the ship travels even when one is asleep. [In contrast, when one is on dry land, whatever kind of life a person leads, at least while sleeping he is not transgressing *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia*.]

The above is in full force wherever the ship may be traveling and whenever it may depart, provided only that it is traveling during the twenty-four hours of Shabbos. In this case, there is the additional factor that one wishes to travel to a land that even non-Jews call "the Holy Land"—not because the United Nations holds this to be so, but because that is how it is written in our holy Torah, which has linked the existence of Eretz Yisrael specifically to the observance of Shabbos, as indicated in many *sedros*, among them—by Divine Providence—also in the *sedra* that we are going to read this Shabbos Kodesh.

The above is already a maximum tragedy, Heaven forbid, but the journey about which you write adds here a tragedy upon a tragedy, for in addition to the two or three Shabbosos that, as written above, are linked to *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* (Heaven forbid), in this case, there is also the desecration of both days of Shavuos in public—the *Yom Tov* when the Ten Commandments were given, given with the full "storm," as it is told in the *Midrashim*, where one of the Ten Commandments is "Observe the day of Shabbos to sanctify it." It is only that we live in a time when one becomes accustomed to all sorts of unbelievable things, so an event such as the one described above can also occur, without anyone raising a voice or chirping in protest.

Naturally, I know that there are those who have taken the responsibility upon themselves—not knowing how a ship is operated, while at the same time considering themselves great experts in the matter—and have permitted the *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* that is conducted in the name of *Klal Yisrael*. And according to what is told, one is to believe that on Shabbos, a Jew stands on the ship in a *tallis* and prays to the Almighty to sanctify the Shabbos, knowing that at that very moment the machinery is being turned on and operated by Jews, telegrams are being written and communications made, cooking and washing, etc., all by Jews, specifically for Jews, and every one of the passengers makes use of it, as well as electricity, water, and all services that are performed through *chillul Shabbos*.

But it is also self-evident that our holy Torah is thereby

## 259

not changed, for our holy Torah is an eternal Torah that the Almighty gave to the Jewish people, and people cannot change it.

Just as our Sages, of blessed memory, have instructed that a Jew must never despair, I still do not want to give up the hope that you, and together with you many, many Jews, will not commit this *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* and *chillul Yom Tov b'farhesia*, and you will cancel your aforementioned journey. And great is the merit of Shabbos to bring you long life and good years, and naturally, the main thing—to have true Jewish Torah-nachas from your children and grandchildren, *shichyu*.

With a blessing for good tidings regarding what is written above.

If, due to the fact that one is canceling the journey so shortly before departure, this is linked to a financial loss, it is understood that taking into account the great prohibition of *b'farhesia*, I will gladly return to you the full sum, with heartfelt thanks for the opportunity to save a Jewish soul from such a tragedy, Heaven forbid, in addition to the fact that it is possible that there will be a few others who will not have the excuse that "if Mrs.... is traveling, it is a sure thing that it is permitted," and will also refrain from it. And it is well known that saving even one Jew is equivalent to saving an entire world.

To your letter, you added a check for *tzedakah* in connection with the journey. This is the first time in my life—and I hope that I will not have to do it again—that I must return such a check. But it is self-evident that I cannot have any connection to a matter that is linked to *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia*, and especially that one wants the *tzedakah* to assist in this *chillul Shabbos*, Heaven forbid. Therefore, the check is returned herewith. I want to hope that you will accept my words, in accordance with today's *sedra*—"You shall keep My Shabbosos... I am Hashem."

(From a letter dated 25 Iyar, 5724)


## בחוקותי

## 260

### Bechukosai

...to write to him regarding the fulfillment of mitzvos: The fulfillment of mitzvos is (also) the path to receiving Hashem’s blessings in all things, as it is stated: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My mitzvos..." and "But if you do not listen to Me..." (see the parsha of Bechukosai at length).

However, Hashem is *erech apayim* (long-suffering) and waits regarding the punishment, *r’l* (Heaven forbid). But who is the "wise man" who would commit a transgression, *ch’v* (Heaven forbid), just because the punishment, *r’l*, will only come after some time?!...

(From a letter dated 15 Kislev, 5747)

## Pirkei Avos — Chapter 6

... He asks for an explanation of the matter of one who learns even a single letter from his teacher—what is the nature of this learning?

Now, in many places throughout the Gemara, we find questions and answers similar to the above. For example, Shabbos 77a (end) and 77b (beginning); likewise, it can be said that this is along the lines of the question in Shabbos 104a. Similarly, in Kiddushin 30a (end), Rav Yosef asks regarding the letter "vav," etc.; Bava Metzia 87a (at the end)—regarding legumes or "and legumes," and many others like these...
