## שיחת ש"פ בחוקותי, כ"ב אייר, תשמ"ו

## 261

### Sicha of Shabbos Parshas Bechukosai, 22 Iyar, 5746

1. Among the primary themes of the days of Sefiras HaOmer is *ahavas Yisrael*:

a) The reason for the unique conduct during the days of Sefiras HaOmer is the mourning for the students of Rabbi Akiva, who "did not show respect to one another," which is to say, a deficiency in the matter of *ahavas Yisrael*. Therefore, during these days, there is a need to increase and multiply *ahavas Yisrael* even more, especially based on the instruction of Rabbi Akiva that the commandment "Love your fellow as yourself" is a "great principle of the Torah."

b) The days of Sefiras HaOmer are a preparation for *Matan Torah*. Therefore, just as the preparation for *Matan Torah* the first time was through the fact that "Israel encamped there,"—"encamped" (*vayichan*) being in the singular form, "like one man with one heart," as it is stated in the *Midrash*: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, said: Since Israel hated discord and loved peace and became one encampment, now is the time for Me to give them My Torah"—it is understood that the preparation for the "time of the giving of our Torah" every single year is likewise through an increase in *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel, "like one man with one heart."

c) One should add to this—by way of *remez*— that the concept of "seven complete weeks shall there be" indicates the perfection (*temimus*) of all seven types within the souls of Israel. As is known, "the totality of the souls of Israel is called a *menorah*, and it has seven lamps, which are the seven levels in the *avodah* of Hashem," the seven *midos*, each of which is comprised of seven ("seven weeks"). This means that the existence of every single Jew touches upon the perfection of the existence of the totality of the Jewish people (just as every day of the days of the *Sefirah* touches upon the perfection of the *Sefiras HaOmer*), and by combining them all together—*ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel—the concept of "seven complete weeks shall there be" is realized: the perfection of the existence of each and every one and the totality of Israel—"*temimus*," and in the full strength of existence—"*tihyena*," "it shall be in its essence," which is the appropriate preparation for receiving the Torah.

2. The aforementioned matter is emphasized most strongly on this *Shabbos*—the *Shabbos* following *Lag B'Omer* (the elevation and perfection—"*vayechulu*"—of all the themes of *Lag B'Omer*), and in the *parsha* of the week—*Parshas Bechukosai*.

## 262

Regarding the first reason, concerning the students of Rabbi Akiva: *Lag B'Omer* is the day on which "they ceased to die," meaning that from *Lag B'Omer* onwards, a new period began for the students of Rabbi Akiva—a conduct of *ahavas Yisrael* in the ultimate perfection.

And another point regarding this:
*Lag B'Omer* is the *yom hilula* of the Rashbi—a student of Rabbi Akiva (one of the students who "established Torah" after *Lag B'Omer*), whose *midos* were "the choicest of the choice of the *midos* of Rabbi Akiva," including and especially the *midah* of *ahavas Yisrael* of Rabbi Akiva ("a great principle in the Torah"), which was emphasized even more strongly in him, as we find that upon exiting the cave (after he had been elevated in Torah to the ultimate degree), he occupied himself first and foremost with *ahavas Yisrael*—"He said: Is there any matter that needs to be rectified, etc.," meaning that he exerted himself for the benefit of the *Kohanim* so that they would not suffer from the burden of the journey.

Furthermore, he exerted himself and worried for the benefit of those who were in a lowly state, etc.—"I am able to exempt the entire world from judgment."

It is also worth noting the story in the *Zohar*: "Once, the world was in need of rain, and they came before the Rashbi... He opened and said: 'A Song of Ascents: Behold, how good and how pleasant it is for brothers to dwell together in unity,'" and through this, rain descended. Beyond what is explained in the *drushei Chassidus* regarding the connection and relevance of the descent of rain to this verse, it can be said (as a possibility, since through this *ahavas Yisrael* will be increased even more) that by doing so, the Rashbi hinted that the matter of "brothers dwelling together in unity," *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel, is the

## 263

"way" and the "vessel" for the drawing down of all blessings, starting with the blessing of rain. In the language of the verse in our *parsha*: "I will give your rains in their time," which includes all blessings—as the *Ramban* explains: "He prioritized the matter of rain because when they come in their time... it will be the cause of health for bodies, and all the fruits will multiply and be blessed through them, as it says: 'The earth will give its produce and the tree of the field will give its fruit'... it is the greatest of blessings." And according to the teaching of the *Baal Shem Tov*: "your rains" (*gishmeichem*) is from the word *gashmiyus* (materiality), meaning the drawing down of blessing (also) in all material matters.

That is to say, the "vessel" for all blessings is—"brothers dwelling together in unity," *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel.

Regarding the second reason, concerning the preparation for *Matan Torah* during the days of *Sefiras HaOmer*: The primary *avodah* of *Sefiras HaOmer* is the refinement of the *midos* of the *nefesh habahamis* (the seven *midos* comprised of seven, forty-nine days), through which, and only then, can the revelation of *Matan Torah* occur. And since the primary *midos* are the first five, it follows that on *Lag B'Omer*, which is the aspect of *Hod shebeHod*, the primary construction of the body of *Ze'er Anpin* is completed, and therefore, the preparation for *Matan Torah*—"like one man with one heart"—is more emphasized.

Regarding the third reason: Note the statement of our Sages: "Rabbi Shimon ben Yochai said: From where do you say that if Israel were missing even one person, the *Shechinah* would not have been revealed to them? Because it is written: 'For on the third day Hashem descended before the eyes of all the people,'" meaning that the Rashbi emphasizes that the matter of *Matan Torah* depends on the existence of each and every one of Israel.

In addition to this, the preparation for *Matan Torah* is emphasized on this *Shabbos* also from the perspective of the *parsha* of the week, *Parshas Bechukosai*—for "Ezra ordained for Israel that they should read the curses in *Toras Kohanim* before *Atzeres*," (and the fact that we read *Parshas Bamidbar* before *Atzeres* is "so as not to place the curses in *Bechukosai* adjacent to *Atzeres*"), from which it is understood that on the *Shabbos* of *Parshas Bechukosai*, the preparation for *Matan Torah*, "like one man with one heart," is more emphasized.

Based on this, it is understood that in these days—the days following *Lag B'Omer*, and as we draw closer and closer to the "time of the giving of our Torah"—there is

## 264

a need to increase with greater strength and greater intensity in all matters of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel.

3. And another most essential point regarding this—concerning our generation, the generation of the footsteps of *Moshiach*, the end of the time of *galus*, with a preface:

One of the primary themes of the Rashbi (the *baal hilula* of *Lag B'Omer*, whose perfection is on this *Shabbos*) is the *Sefer HaZohar*, "your composition," which, "through this composition of yours, which is the *Sefer HaZohar*... they will emerge from *galus* with mercy," meaning that the mission of the Rashbi is to bring about the redemption of each and every Jew and the totality of Israel, together with the redemption of the *Shechinah*, as the Rashbi says: "Wherever they (Israel) were exiled, the *Shechinah* is with them... and even when they are destined to be redeemed, the *Shechinah* is with them."

Now, since the cause of the *galus* is the opposite of the matter of *ahavas Yisrael* (baseless [hatred]), it is understood that there is a need to nullify the cause of the *galus* through an increase in *ahavas Yisrael* to the point of *ahavas chinam* (baseless love), and when the cause is nullified, the effect—the *galus*—is nullified automatically.

It should be added that when the conduct of Israel in practice is in the manner of "Love your fellow as yourself," then the love of "your fellow"—"your fellow and your father's fellow do not forsake, this is the Holy One, Blessed be He"—is certainly revealed in practice for each and every Jew,

As the Rashbi says: "How beloved are Israel before the Holy One, Blessed be He," and as it is stated in the *Zohar*—"your composition"—(the passage of the *Zohar* that we say in *Tikkun Leil Shavuos*): "Rabbi Shimon rejoiced and said... We depend on love... 'I have loved you,' says Hashem"—

And when the love of the Holy One, Blessed be He, for Israel is in revelation, then certainly and surely He will bring them out of *galus* ("And Hashem your G-d will return your captivity") immediately, "He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye,"

And as the *remez* that through the drawing down and revelation of the "Master of the World" (*Alufo shel Olam*—the *Aleph*) into the "exile" (*golah*), the "exile" (*golah*) becomes "redemption" (*geulah*).

4. Now, the matter of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel is revealed and expressed—first and foremost—when many of Israel gather together in one place, "like one man with one heart," and furthermore, the purpose and

## 265

goal of the gathering is—so that "each man will help his fellow" to awaken and strengthen one another in all good actions, and especially—in the great principle of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel.

Especially when one connects this gathering with a meal in the literal sense, including and especially saying "*L'chaim*" over wine—a thing that adds even more to the movement of closeness, "Great is the sip that brings close."

And as is known the saying of the *Alter Rebbe* regarding the great virtue of a *farbrengen*—"a note that descended from the heavens, etc."—like the parable of the father who sees the "good conduct of his children in love, brotherhood, peace, and friendship, each fulfilling the will of his fellow, and each worrying for the good of his friend as for his own good, etc., then the father is filled with pleasure and *nachas* from the conduct of his children, and he performs wonders to fulfill their requests, etc." (as mentioned above (section 2) that through "brothers dwelling together in unity" all matters of blessing are drawn down).

5. However, since during the days of the *Sefirah* there are restrictions regarding holding a meal of celebration, and within this itself there are differences of custom regarding the time after *Lag B'Omer*, etc., one must choose a time suitable for all opinions, so that each and every Jew, from all circles, etc., each according to the custom and tradition of his ancestors, will be able to participate in this *farbrengen*.

Therefore, the time suitable for this is—the day of *Shabbos*, which, according to all opinions, has no concern or doubt about the matter, for the day of *Shabbos* has no "sadness with it," and on the contrary—"on the day of your rejoicing, these are the *Shabbosos*."

And there is an extra emphasis on the upcoming *Shabbos*—*Shabbos Mevarchim* for the month of *Sivan*, the "third month," and in the calendar of this year—*Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan*, and the *parsha* of the week—*Parshas Bamidbar*:

a) *Shabbos Mevarchim* (in public and gathering) the "third month": The "third month" indicates the matter of peace and unity, as is known that the unique virtue of the number three is—the connection and inclusion of two matters that might be in opposition to each other. This is also the connection to the general matter of *Matan Torah*—"The threefold Torah... in the third month"—for "all

## 266

the Torah was given to make peace in the world." Therefore, on *Shabbos Mevarchim* the third month—from which blessing is drawn down for all the days of the "third month"—the matter of peace and unity is most emphasized.

b) *Erev Rosh Chodesh* of the "third month": The matter of *Rosh Chodesh*—its beginning on *Erev Rosh Chodesh* (the day of *Shabbos*) after midday, which is why we do not say "*Tzidkascha Tzedek*" at *Mincha* of *Shabbos*. Furthermore, since sometimes one can pray the "*Maariv* of *Motzaei Shabbos* on *Shabbos*," at which time one prays the *Rosh Chodesh* prayer on the day of *Shabbos*—"*Ya'aleh V'Yavo*, etc., our remembrance, etc., and the remembrance of all Your people the House of Israel." It follows that on the coming *Shabbos*, *Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan*, there is already the matter of *Rosh Chodesh Sivan*, at which time there was the matter of unity (as a preparation for *Matan Torah*) in actual practice—"In the third month... on this day (*Rosh Chodesh*) they came... and Israel encamped there," "like one man with one heart."

c) The *parsha* of the week, *Parshas Bamidbar*: The content of *Parshas Bamidbar* ("We always read *Parshas Bamidbar Sinai* before *Atzeres*") is—the census of the Children of Israel, meaning the perfection of all the Children of Israel in a manner of the unity of Israel—for the "census" is in a manner where all of Israel in the census are equal; the greatest of the great is not counted as more than one, and the smallest of the small is not counted as less than one,

And the census, its cause is *ahavas Yisrael* (of the Holy One, Blessed be He—the cause of *ahavas Yisrael* for one another—"He loves what the Beloved loves")—"Because of their affection before Him, He counts them, etc."

From this it is understood that the upcoming *Shabbos*, *Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Bamidbar*, *Mevarchim HaChodesh* and *Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan*, is the time most suitable for emphasizing the unity of Israel.

6. In light of all that has been said above—comes the following proposal and request, a soulful request:

On the upcoming *Shabbos*, *Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Bamidbar*, *Mevarchim HaChodesh* and *Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan*, at the time of *Mincha* (when the matter of the unity of *Rosh Chodesh Sivan* already begins (as above in section 5))—let many of Israel gather in every place, men, women, and children, "with our young and with our old, etc., with our sons and with our daughters," "brothers dwelling together in unity," for a gathering of friends, up to a meal in the literal sense ("Great

## 267

is the sip that brings close")—men separately and women separately (obviously and simply),
in which they will speak words of Torah in general, and especially—on the matters of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel,
—starting from what is explicit in the Written Torah: "Love your fellow as yourself," and also in the Oral Torah: "Rabbi Akiva says this is a great principle in the Torah," and more than that: "This is the entire Torah, and the rest is its commentary," and also the details of the matters in the *Sefer Mishneh Torah* of the *Rambam*,, the book of "*Halachos Halachos*," *halacha* for practice, up to the explanation of our *Rabbeinu HaZaken* in the *Sefer Tanya* on the greatness of the virtue and wonder of the matter of *ahavas Yisrael*, and similarly in the books of many of the great ones of Israel that have been accepted in all the dispersions of Israel—
including—the emphasis on the matter, that the increase in *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel nullifies the cause of the *galus*, and automatically the (effect) *galus* is also nullified.
[Note: Regarding the content of the words about *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel—for "not all intellects and opinions are equal, and the intellect of one person is not moved and awakened by what the intellect of his fellow is moved," there are those who will be moved more by an explanation in the *nigleh* of Torah, and there are those who will be moved more by an explanation in the *pnimiyus* of Torah; therefore, one must find the explanations and letters suitable for each place and circle according to its nature. However, first and foremost, one must emphasize the content and the point of the matter, in a way that is relevant to each and every Jew, even to one who wants to learn "the entire Torah (of *ahavas Yisrael*) on one foot"—as Hillel said (in response to the non-Jew who said to him "Convert me on the condition that you teach me the entire Torah while I am standing on one foot"): "That which is hateful to you, do not do to your fellow ('Love your fellow as yourself')—this is the entire Torah, and the rest is its commentary!"]
And furthermore and essentially—that "each man will help his fellow," to encourage each man his fellow (and woman her fellow) to increase with greater strength and greater intensity in all matters of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel.
And in those places where, for various reasons, it is difficult to do all this on the day of *Shabbos*—they should do it on the weekdays, on *Rosh Chodesh Sivan* and the like (in a permitted manner, etc.).

7. Surely they will publicize the matters in every place,

## 268

[And it is understood that in this matter there is no necessity to say the words "in the name of their author," but rather, in a style that will bring greater benefit in the actual fulfillment of the matters, especially since this is not a novel thing, but matters that are explicit in the Written Torah and the Oral Torah, and consequently, anyone who contemplates the matter—will come by himself to the aforementioned conclusion, and will do so ultimately because his own intellect commands him so],
and they will occupy themselves with this with much energy, vitality, and enthusiasm, etc. (and it goes without saying—not in the manner of "a commandment of men learned by rote"), taking into account the fact that this is a soulful matter regarding a special and extraordinary thing, etc. (and therefore, even the speaking now about this matter is at a time that is not according to the usual—not at the end of the *farbrengen*, as is usual in such cases, but at the beginning and start of the *farbrengen*), because of the need of the hour, etc.

8. And regarding the practical:
In order that the actions in this matter should be in an orderly fashion and with great success—there is a need to begin in good time, starting from publicizing the matter in every place, up to organizing the details of the matters in actual practice in every place.
Therefore, we awaken about this on the day of *Shabbos*, "we attend to the needs of the public on *Shabbos*,"—so that they will utilize all the days of the week (starting from *Motzaei Shabbos*) to occupy themselves with the necessary preparations for this, in the manner of "every day, one does his work,"
meaning, the general approach should be in ways of pleasantness and in ways of peace ("ways of *Shabbos*"), and within this itself—each day according to its unique manner of *avodah*, "ways of pleasantness" from the aspect of the *midah* of *Chesed* (Sunday), "ways of pleasantness" from the aspect of the *midah* of *Gevurah* (Monday), and similarly throughout all six days of the week,
up to the day of *Shabbos* itself, and especially at the time of "*Rava D'Ravin*"—at which time all those gathering and *farbrenging* in every place and location will unite, "as one,"
for, even though "the time of the entry of *Shabbos*... is in every country according to the time of the days and nights in it," and consequently, the *farbrengens* that will take place in every place and location at the time of *Mincha* of *Shabbos* will not be down here on earth at the exact same hour—yet, since the "time of favor from above" (a result of the unity of Israel) "is above the constraints of place and time," it follows that all those *farbrenging* in all places will unite as one truly.

9. And another point regarding the practical preparations—in connection with the financial expense:
These actions, like all actions, involve financial expense. And the question is known [as is customary to use—by way of wit—in the language of our Sages] "From where do we have the money?"...
Now, first and foremost, there is the answer of

## 269

"Torah is truth," that the matter of "money" is learned from a verse in the Torah, meaning, that there is a giving of strength from the Torah for everything related to the need for this "money," and consequently, surely enough money will be found for these actions in every place—in that very place,
and there is an extra virtue in this—as is known that all matters of holiness are not in the manner of "for free" ("which we ate in Egypt for free"), for the giving from one's own money indicates that the matter touches him, etc., to the point that he participates in the matter also with his money, and consequently, he occupies himself with it with more vitality, etc.
However, if there is a place where there might be some deficit, G-d forbid, in these actions because of the financial expense of the matter—then, after the completion of the action (and the accounting), they should notify a central place what is the sum that was required for organizing the *farbrengen* and the party, etc., and from all the central places they will notify here, and without a vow, they will send from here for the expenses of the matter, with joy and a good heart.

10. And may it be the will that the acceptance of the good resolution (even before they begin to occupy themselves with the matter in actual practice) will bring about immediately the "reward" that belongs to the action of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unity of Israel—the nullification of the *galus*,
and simply—that immediately and truly we merit the true and complete redemption through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*,
and especially—that we are now at the conclusion of the *Shabbos*, in proximity to *Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh*, the "meal of King David, *Moshiach*,"
and then, when the upcoming *Shabbos* arrives—a "great *farbrengen*" of all the Children of Israel will take place, "a great congregation shall return here,"
and "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," and "Moses and Aaron with them," and the Rashbi with them, and all the *tzaddikim* and *Nesi'im* of Israel, up to *Kvod Kedushas Moreinu V'Rabbeinu* the *Nasi* of our generation—for *tzaddikim* (and up to "and Your people are all *tzaddikim*") rise for resurrection immediately,
and the "head of the speakers" at this *farbrengen* will be—*Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, who will teach Torah to all the people (including the Patriarchs and Moses our Teacher, etc.)—"A new Torah shall go forth from Me," the *pnimiyus* of the Torah, and in a manner of vision,

## 270

and then there will also be the census of the Children of Israel—the content of *Parshas Bamidbar*—in ultimate perfection, the "tenth census," through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, "the first redeemer is the last redeemer,"
in our days, truly.

## אימוץ ילדים

## Adoption of Children



The question of adopting a child—specifically, the halachic and spiritual implications of such an act—is a profound matter that touches upon the fundamental connection between parents and children.

In the Torah’s perspective, the bond between a parent and a child is not merely a biological or social construct; it is a spiritual reality. When a person raises a child, even if that child was not born to them, the Torah recognizes the depth of this relationship. As the Sages state, "Whoever teaches their neighbor's child Torah, it is as if they gave birth to them" (Sanhedrin 19b). This principle extends beyond the realm of Torah study to the entirety of the child's upbringing and development.

When a couple adopts a child, they are not merely performing an act of kindness or fulfilling a social need. They are entering into a sacred responsibility—a form of *avodah*—whereby they become the conduits for the child's *neshamah* to manifest in this world. By providing the child with a home, love, and a foundation in Torah and *mitzvos*, the adoptive parents are, in a very real sense, "birthing" the child into a life of *kedushah*.

It is important to note that while the biological connection is a natural order established by Hashem, the spiritual connection forged through the dedication of raising a child is a testament to the power of human *bechirah* (free choice). Through this *avodah*, the parents elevate the child, and in doing so, they elevate themselves. The child, in turn, becomes an integral part of the family, sharing in the family's *mesorah* and spiritual legacy.

Ultimately, the act of adoption, when undertaken with the proper *kavanah* and a commitment to raising the child in the path of Torah and *mitzvos*, is a profound expression of *chesed*. It reflects the way Hashem relates to the world—constantly nurturing and sustaining His creations—and serves as a powerful example of how we, as His partners, can bring more light and *Elokus* into the world.

## אתכפיא ואתהפכא

## אתכפיא ואתהפכא



The concept of *iskafya* (subjugation) and *is'hapcha* (transformation) is well known. *Iskafya* is the initial stage of *avodah*, where one suppresses the *sitra achra* and prevents it from expressing itself in action, speech, or thought. *Is'hapcha* is the higher level, where the *sitra achra* itself is transformed into holiness, such that the very energy that previously sought to pull a person toward the mundane is now directed toward *avodas Hashem*.

Seemingly, one might ask: If *is'hapcha* is the ultimate goal—to the point that the *Tanya* states that the *tzaddik* has no *yetzer hara* at all, because he has transformed it into good—why is *iskafya* necessary at all? Why not simply strive for *is'hapcha* from the outset?

But in truth, the order of *avodah* is fixed: *iskafya* must precede *is'hapcha*. One cannot reach the level of transforming the *sitra achra* without first establishing the foundation of *iskafya*. Just as a person must first learn to control their impulses before they can refine their character, so too in the realm of *avodah*, the *bitul* achieved through *iskafya* acts as the vessel that allows for the light of *is'hapcha* to be revealed. 

This is the deeper meaning of the *maamar* that "the *yetzer hara* is only conquered through the words of Torah." Through the *avodah* of *iskafya*, a person creates a state of *dveikus* with Hashem, which then provides the strength to achieve *is'hapcha*. It is not that *iskafya* is merely a temporary measure; rather, it is the essential process through which the *nefesh habahamit* is prepared to be elevated and transformed into a vehicle for *kedushah*.

## לשמה

## Levels in the Avodah of Lishmah

The concept of *lishmah*—performing a mitzvah for its own sake—is not a single, uniform level. Rather, there are various levels in the *avodah* of *lishmah*.

At the most basic level, *lishmah* means performing a mitzvah without the intent of receiving a reward, as the Mishnah states: "Do not be like servants who serve their master for the sake of receiving a reward." This is the initial stage of *avodah*, where one removes the element of self-interest from the performance of the mitzvah.

Beyond this, there is a higher level of *lishmah*: performing the mitzvah out of *ahavah* and *yirah* for Hashem. Here, the *avodah* is not merely the absence of a desire for reward, but the presence of a positive, internal drive. The *chossid* is moved by the reality of Hashem, and the mitzvah becomes the vessel through which that *ahavah* and *yirah* are expressed.

Yet, even this is not the ultimate *lishmah*. The highest level is when the *avodah* is performed with such complete *bitul* that the *chossid* does not perceive themselves as an independent entity performing a service at all. In this state, the mitzvah is not something the person "does"; rather, it is the *ratzon* of Hashem being fulfilled through them. This is the *avodah* of *yechidah*, where the *neshamah* is so bound up in *dveikus* with the *Ein Sof* that the distinction between the one who serves and the One being served is transcended.

## ממון

(Like one of the parts of a person).

(Regarding money that is necessary for the avodah of Hashem, there is no issue of "serving in order to receive a reward").

## מצרים

## Mitzrayim

 The Exodus from Mitzrayim was not through an angel, nor through a messenger. In the redemption from Mitzrayim, Bnei Yisrael became forever liberated from that state of slavery, and the servitude of the [subsequent] exiles is not of the same category as the exile of Mitzrayim. The spiritual difficulty of the exile of Mitzrayim was greater than that of the other exiles. "The Mitzrim treated us harshly" — the point of evil was directed against the *kotzo shel yud*. All the kingdoms are named after Mitzrayim, etc. Whether the plagues affected only the four elements or also the *chomer hayuli* (prime matter). The redemption from Mitzrayim was the redemption of the point of goodness and the point of Yiddishkeit from the point of evil. An eternal redemption. He revealed Himself to them, etc., in His glory and His essence. The Exodus from Mitzrayim was a spiritual redemption through miracles beyond miracles. The Exodus from Mitzrayim was akin to a birth. While in Mitzrayim, Yisrael were distinguished by their language, their clothing, etc., yet on the other hand, they were "a nation within a nation." An exodus from slavery to a transcendent freedom. The exodus of all of Yisrael in a single moment. The Exodus from Mitzrayim occurs every day; an exodus from *meitzarim* (limitations) and boundaries.

See also: *Ananei HaKavod*, *Pesach*.

## משכן

## Mishkan

 The parameters of Moshe’s service in the Kehunah during the seven days of the inauguration (Miluim). Two aspects: a house for Hashem for the offerings, and the "Ohel Moed" as a place designated for communication with Moshe. Whether the concept of "And I will meet with you" applies only to the Mishkan or also to the Beis Hamikdash. Levels of the indwelling and dveikus of the Shechinah in the Mikdash. The matters involved in the inauguration of the Mishkan and the Mizbe'ach were in the category of a temporary instruction (hora'as sha'ah).

See also: [ftnref_bgd] Bigdei Kehunah. [ftnref_moshe] Moshe. [ftnref_kodesh] Kodesh Hakodashim.

## ר&quot;ח ניסן

## Rosh Chodesh Nissan

 (That day took ten crowns). - (The New Year for kings and for the festivals). (It falls on the same day of the week as the first day of Chol HaMoed Pesach. From that time on, according to all opinions, one inquires and expounds upon the laws of Pesach).


## ב' ניסן

## 2 Nissan



The passing of the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation, on the second of Nissan, requires us to reflect on the significance of this day in the context of the *avodah* of a *chossid* and the *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe.

The *Gemara* states that "the righteous are called alive even after their death." This is not merely a statement of spiritual survival, but a fundamental principle regarding the nature of the *tzaddik’s* influence. The *avodah* of the *tzaddik*—his *bitul*, his *mesiras nefesh*, and his *dveikus* to Hashem—does not cease when he departs from this world. On the contrary, his influence becomes even more internalized and accessible to those who are connected to him.

When we speak of the *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe, we are not referring to a historical connection to a figure of the past. Rather, we are speaking of a living, ongoing engagement with the *sichos*, the *maamarim*, and the directives that the Rebbe left for us. This is the *avodah* of the *dor hashvi'i*—to take the light of *Chassidus* and bring it into the world, transforming the world into a *dirah b'tachtonim*.

The second of Nissan serves as a *hisorerus* for every *chossid*. It is a time to pause and evaluate: to what extent is my *avodah* aligned with the path the Rebbe paved? How am I internalizing the *kavanah* of the *mitzvos* and the *taanug* of *dveikus* that the Rebbe demanded of us?

Ultimately, the goal is *is'hapcha*—to transform the darkness of *galus* into the light of *Geulah*. This is achieved through the *avodah* of *tashuvah* and *tefillah*, performed with the strength and the *koach* that the Rebbe continues to provide from above. May we merit to see the fulfillment of the Rebbe’s promise, "Immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*," with the coming of Moshiach now.


## י&quot;א ניסן

## 11 Nissan


## י&quot;ג ניסן

## 13 Nissan

 The concept of the 13th of Nissan is that it is the day before the eve of Pesach, and it is the time for *bedikas chametz* (the search for *chametz*).

The inner meaning of this is that *chametz* represents *yeshus* (self-centeredness) and *gaavah* (pride), which are the antithesis of *matzah*—the symbol of *bitul* (self-nullification). The *avodah* of *bedikas chametz* is to search for and remove this *yeshus* from all the hidden corners of one’s heart, even in those places that one does not usually notice or pay attention to.

This search must be conducted with a *ner* (candle), which represents the *neshamah*, as it is written, "The candle of Hashem is the soul of man." Through the light of the *neshamah*, one illuminates the dark corners of the *nefesh habehamis* to identify and nullify any remaining *chametz*.

Ultimately, the goal of this *avodah* is to reach a state of complete *bitul*, which is the preparation required to receive the revelation of the *Ohr Ein Sof* that is drawn down during the days of Pesach. By clearing away the *chametz* of the ego, one creates the necessary vessel to experience the true freedom of *Yetziyas Mitzrayim* in a way that is internalized and lasting.

## שבועות, חג השבועות

## Shavuos, Chag HaShavuos

 Regarding the parameters of permitting the *minchah chadashah* (new grain offering) through the *shtei halechem* (two loaves). The *shtei halechem* is human food, whereas the *omer* is animal food. The *shtei halechem* is *chametz*, representing *is'hapcha*. The *shtei halechem* represents the unification of the bread with the sheep in spiritual *avodah*. The *shtei halechem* represents *Torah Shebichtav* and *Torah Shebe'al Peh*, the *nistar* of Torah and the *nigleh* of Torah. The *shtei halechem* as a *minchah chadashah*. Determining the date of *Chag HaShavuos* for one who crossed the International Date Line during the days of *Sefirah*.

## שבת הגדול

## Shabbos HaGadol


## שבת מברכים

## Shabbos Mevarchim

 The concept of Shabbos Mevarchim — blessing the new month — is that it serves as the source of blessing for the entire month. As is well known, the month of the year corresponds to the soul’s service in the world, and the blessing of the month provides the strength and vitality for this service throughout the coming days.

This is particularly relevant when we consider the connection between the specific month and the avodah of the Chassid. Through the act of blessing the month on Shabbos, we draw down the energy of the *Ein Sof* into the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, ensuring that the *avodah* of the month is performed with *bitul* and *kavanah*. 

Seemingly, one might ask: if the blessing is drawn down on Shabbos, why is it necessary to engage in *avodah* throughout the weekdays? But in truth, the blessing of Shabbos is merely the potential; the *avodah* of the weekdays is the actualization. This is the mechanism of *ratzo v'shov* — the soul ascends to *dveikus* on Shabbos, and then descends into the mundane reality of the week to transform it, thereby revealing the *Elokus* that was latent within the blessing. 

And with this we can understand the importance of *hiskashrus* to the Rebbe during this time. By connecting to the Nasi of the generation, one gains the clarity to channel the blessing of the month into practical *mitzvos* and *avodah*, ensuring that the entire month is infused with the light of the *maamarim* and *sichos* that guide our path.

## שלמה, רש&quot;י

## Shlomo, Rashi

 In his commentary on the Torah, it is his practice to explain rather than to copy the language of our Sages verbatim.

 His commentary is not a book of halacha.

 When he does not explain his words, it is because he relies on what has already been clarified in the preceding verses.

 Even if it is the way of Scripture to use the letter *vav* in place of "or," it is a matter requiring study whether Rashi would also write in this manner, given that he wrote his commentary in clear and precise language.

 He brings examples in his commentary from the current and the commonplace.

## תורה עבודה וגמילות חסדים

## Torah, Avodah, and Gemilas Chasadim



The Mishnah in Pirkei Avos states: "The world stands on three things: on Torah, on Avodah, and on Gemilas Chasadim." 

Seemingly, we must understand the order of these three pillars. Why is Torah mentioned first, followed by Avodah, and finally Gemilas Chasadim? Furthermore, what is the internal connection between these three, and how do they collectively sustain the world?

To understand this, we must first clarify the nature of each of these three pillars.

Torah represents the wisdom of Hashem, which is entirely transcendent. Through the study of Torah, a person connects their intellect to the Divine intellect. This is an act of "reception"—the person draws down the light of Elokus into their own mind.

Avodah, by contrast, represents the service of the heart—specifically, tefillah. Unlike Torah, which is the descent of Divine wisdom to man, Avodah is the ascent of the soul from below to above. It is the process of refining one's own character and emotions, bringing them into a state of bitul before Hashem.

Gemilas Chasadim represents the manifestation of this holiness in the world of action. It is not merely a private act of piety, but the extension of one's own goodness to another. It is the bridge between the internal state of the individual and the reality of the world around them.

Thus, the order is precise: First, one must engage in Torah to acquire the proper perspective and Divine wisdom. Second, one must engage in Avodah to internalize that wisdom and transform one's own heart. And third, one must engage in Gemilas Chasadim to project that transformation outward, thereby sustaining the world.

## תרמוד

## Tarmod

 The Gemara states, "The people of Tarmod are not to be accepted [for conversion]." The commentators discuss the reason for this: some say it is because they were involved in the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash, while others say it is because they were involved in the burning of the Beis Hamikdash. 

On the face of it, we must understand: why is this specific group singled out? Throughout the generations, many nations and individuals participated in the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash. Why is it that specifically the people of Tarmod are prohibited from entering the congregation of Hashem, even if they were to seek conversion?

Furthermore, the Gemara concludes that the reason they are not accepted is because they are "mamzerim" (illegitimate). This requires explanation: how does their involvement in the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash render them mamzerim?

But in truth, we can understand this by first examining the spiritual root of Tarmod. The name "Tarmod" is associated with the concept of *meridah* (rebellion). Their essence is one of opposition to the holiness of the Beis Hamikdash, which is the point of connection between Hashem and the Jewish people. Because they represent the absolute antithesis of this connection, their very existence is a negation of the sanctity of the Jewish people. Therefore, they are fundamentally incompatible with the holiness of the Jewish nation, to the extent that they are categorized as mamzerim—those who are excluded from the congregation of Hashem.

## שמיני

## Shemini

(Sometimes it is read eight times).
9:8-9 And Aharon approached... and the sons of Aharon brought...
9:9 And he dipped his finger in the blood...
9:12 And he slaughtered the burnt offering, and they presented it to him... (and Rashi: an expression of extending and offering).
And he threw it upon the altar:
9:13 And they presented the burnt offering to him...
9:14 And he burned the fat upon the burnt offering:
9:18 And the sons of Aharon presented it to him...
9:23 In Rashi, s.v. "And he came": Why did Moshe enter with Aharon... and the Shechinah descended...
In Rashi, s.v. "And they went out": All seven days of the inauguration... he said to him... Aharon my brother...
9:23-24 And the glory of Hashem appeared... and fire went out from before Hashem...
9:24 And all the people saw and sang (and Rashi):
10:1 And they offered strange fire before Hashem...
10:2 And fire went out from before Hashem...
10:3 This is what Hashem spoke... "By those who are near to Me I will be sanctified" (and Rashi: I knew that it would be sanctified...):
10:10-11 To distinguish... to teach... by the hand of Moshe:
11:8 And you shall not touch their carcass (and Rashi: Could it be that Yisroel are warned...):
11:43 Do not make yourselves detestable...
11:44 And you shall sanctify yourselves and you shall be holy...

## הלכות תמורה

## Laws of Temurah

At the end of the laws, [it is stated]: "Even though all the *chukim*..." [it is] appropriate to contemplate them.....

[Chukim have no revealed reason]:.

It appears to me that this is the meaning of the verse, "Then it and its exchange shall be..." — the Torah descends to the depth of human thought....

Most of the laws of the Torah are nothing but counsel... and to straighten all deeds:.

[Conclusion of Sefer Korbanos in Hilchos Temurah]:.
